  <script type="text/javascript">
    (function() {
        var contextPath = '/jira';
        var eventBuffer = [];

        function printDeprecatedMsg() {
            if (console && console.warn) {
                console.warn('DEPRECATED JS - contextPath global variable has been deprecated since 7.4.0. Use `wrm/context-path` module instead.');
            }
        }

        function sendEvent(analytics, postfix) {
            analytics.send({
                name: 'js.globals.contextPath.' + postfix
            });
        }

        function sendDeprecatedEvent(postfix) {
            try {
                var analytics = require('jira/analytics');
                if (eventBuffer.length) {
                    eventBuffer.forEach(function(value) {
                        sendEvent(analytics, value);
                    });
                    eventBuffer = [];
                }

                if (postfix) {
                    sendEvent(analytics, postfix);
                }
            } catch(ex) {
                eventBuffer.push(postfix);
                setTimeout(sendDeprecatedEvent, 1000);
            }
        }

        Object.defineProperty(window, 'contextPath', {
            get: function() {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('get');
                return contextPath;
            },
            set: function(value) {
                printDeprecatedMsg();
                sendDeprecatedEvent('set');
                contextPath = value;
            }
        });
    })();

</script>

                   <ul class="property-list"> 
                    <li id="rowForcustomfield_12310120" class="item"> 
                     <div class="wrap"> 
                      <strong title="Lucene Fields" class="name">Lucene Fields:</strong> 
                      <div id="customfield_12310120-val" class="value type-multicheckboxes" data-fieldtype="multicheckboxes" data-fieldtypecompletekey="com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.customfieldtypes:multicheckboxes">

              <div id="descriptionmodule" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="descriptionmodule_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>
                <h2 class="toggle-title">Description</h2>
               </div>
               <div class="mod-content">
                <div id="description-val" class="field-ignore-highlight"> 
                 <div class="user-content-block"> 
                  <p>WhitespaceTokenizer uses <a href="http://docs.oracle.com/javase/8/docs/api/java/lang/Character.html#isWhitespace-int-" class="external-link" rel="nofollow">Character.isWhitespace </a> to decide what is whitespace. Here's a pertinent excerpt:</p> 
                  <blockquote>
                   <p>It is a Unicode space character (SPACE_SEPARATOR, LINE_SEPARATOR, or PARAGRAPH_SEPARATOR) but is not also a non-breaking space ('\u00A0', '\u2007', '\u202F')</p>
                  </blockquote> 
                  <p>Perhaps Character.isWhitespace should have been called isLineBreakableWhitespace?</p> 
                  <p>I think WhitespaceTokenizer should tokenize on this. I am aware it's easy to work around but why leave this trap in by default?</p> 
                 </div> 
                </div> 
               </div>
              </div>
              <div id="dnd-metadata" class="module toggle-wrap">
               <div id="dnd-metadata_heading" class="mod-header">
                <ul class="ops"></ul>

\u003cspan class=\'commentdate_14985076_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'02\\/Nov\\/15 11:17\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2015-11-02T11:17:26+0000\'\u003e02\\/Nov\\/15 11:17\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    My personal opinion on this: \\n \\n\\t The thing is called WhitespaceTokenizer, so it should do what the name says (split on isWhitespace). \\n\\t If we want something else, maybe provide a separate CharTokenizer implementation that also splits on NBSP \\n \\n\\n\\n In general, whitespace tokenizer is not used for \\\"classical\\\" fulltext. For this type of text one would better use StandardTokenizer, ICU\'s Tokenizers or the language specific ones for Chinese or Japan. People using WhitespaceTokenizer are more those people which have very special types of fields, like a list of whitespace-separated tokens used for facetting or stuff like a list of product numbers. These types of tokens were always good to handle with WhitespaceTokenizer. If you wanted to keep your facet tokens together, you were able to use NBSP! So a change here would be a break for those apps   \\n\\n So I would just update documentation to explain what this thing does (splitting on whitespace and not on spaces in general). \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Jack Krupansky\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_14985540_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'02\\/Nov\\/15 17:03\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2015-11-02T17:03:09+0000\'\u003e02\\/Nov\\/15 17:03\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e   - \u003cspan class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"Jack Krupansky - 02\\/Nov\\/15 17:34\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003e+1 for using the Unicode definition of white space rather than the (odd) Java definition. From a Solr user perspective, the fact that Java is used for implementation under the hood should be irrelevant. That said, the Javadoc for WhitespaceTokenizer#isTokenChar does explicitly refer to isWhitespace already.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe term \\\"non-breaking white space\\\" explicitly refers to line breaking and has no mention of tokens in either Unicode or traditional casual usage.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eFrom a Solr user perspective, there is like zero value to having NBSP from HTML web pages being treated as if it were not traditional white space.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eFrom a Solr user perspective, the primary use of whitespace tokenizer is to avoid the fact that standard tokenizer breaks on various special characters such as occur in product numbers.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eOne of the ongoing problems in the Solr community is the sheer amount of time spent explaining nuances and gotchas, even if they do happen to be documented somewhere in the fine print - no sane user reads the fine print anyway. No Solr user actually uses WhitespaceTokenizer directly - they reference WhitespaceTokenizerFactory, and then having to drop down to Lucene and Java for doc is way too much to ask a typical Solr user. Our collective goal should be to minimize nuances and gotchas (IMHO.)\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIn short, the benefits to Solr users for NBSP being tokenized as white space seem to outweigh any minor use cases for treating it as non-white space. A compatibility mode can be provided if those minor use cases are considered truly worthwhile.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eUgh... there are plenty of other places in doc for other tokenizers and filters that refer to \\\"whitespace\\\" and need to address this same issue, either to treat NBSP as white space or doc the nuance\\/gotcha much more thoroughly and effectively.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eOTOH... an alternative view... having so many un\\/poorly-documented nuances and gotchas is money in the pockets of consultants and a great argument in favor of Solr users maximizing the employment of Solr consultants.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n                                            \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"jkrupan\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_14985540_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=jkrupan\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"jkrupan\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Jack Krupansky\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_14985540_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'02\\/Nov\\/15 17:03\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2015-11-02T17:03:09+0000\'\u003e02\\/Nov\\/15 17:03\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e   - \u003cspan class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"Jack Krupansky - 02\\/Nov\\/15 17:34\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e                   +1 for using the Unicode definition of white space rather than the (odd) Java definition. From a Solr user perspective, the fact that Java is used for implementation under the hood should be irrelevant. That said, the Javadoc for WhitespaceTokenizer#isTokenChar does explicitly refer to isWhitespace already. \\n\\n The term \\\"non-breaking white space\\\" explicitly refers to line breaking and has no mention of tokens in either Unicode or traditional casual usage. \\n\\n From a Solr user perspective, there is like zero value to having NBSP from HTML web pages being treated as if it were not traditional white space. \\n\\n From a Solr user perspective, the primary use of whitespace tokenizer is to avoid the fact that standard tokenizer breaks on various special characters such as occur in product numbers. \\n\\n One of the ongoing problems in the Solr community is the sheer amount of time spent explaining nuances and gotchas, even if they do happen to be documented somewhere in the fine print - no sane user reads the fine print anyway. No Solr user actually uses WhitespaceTokenizer directly - they reference WhitespaceTokenizerFactory, and then having to drop down to Lucene and Java for doc is way too much to ask a typical Solr user. Our collective goal should be to minimize nuances and gotchas (IMHO.) \\n\\n In short, the benefits to Solr users for NBSP being tokenized as white space seem to outweigh any minor use cases for treating it as non-white space. A compatibility mode can be provided if those minor use cases are considered truly worthwhile. \\n\\n Ugh... there are plenty of other places in doc for other tokenizers and filters that refer to \\\"whitespace\\\" and need to address this same issue, either to treat NBSP as white space or doc the nuance\\/gotcha much more thoroughly and effectively. \\n\\n OTOH... an alternative view... having so many un\\/poorly-documented nuances and gotchas is money in the pockets of consultants and a great argument in favor of Solr users maximizing the employment of Solr consultants. title=\'02\\/Nov\\/15 17:37\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2015-11-02T17:37:30+0000\'\u003e02\\/Nov\\/15 17:37\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    I don\'t think we should make yet another definition of whitespace for java, there are already effectively 3 (Java isWhiteSpace(), java isSpaceChar(), and unicode whitespace): I think it would be better to just expose \\\"unicode whitespace space\\\" for situations like this. \\n\\n java isSpaceChar is impractical, lets not even go there: it does not include controls such as tabs. so isSpaceChar(\'\\\\t\') == false and so on. \\n\\n unicode whitespace is probably more useful and already well-defined: \\n\\n  http:\\/\\/icu-project.org\\/apiref\\/icu4j\\/com\\/ibm\\/icu\\/lang\\/UCharacter.html#isUWhiteSpace%28int%29  \\n http:\\/\\/unicode.org\\/cldr\\/utility\\/list-unicodeset.jsp?a=[:White_Space=Yes: ] \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_14985598_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'02\\/Nov\\/15 17:43\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2015-11-02T17:43:09+0000\'\u003e02\\/Nov\\/15 17:43\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003eSo maybe we should solve this problem by adding some documentation?\u003c\\/p\u003e\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eIf the vast majority (like 90%+) of users that currently use WhitespaceTokenizer would want to tokenize on it, then I don\'t think documentation is sufficient at all.  Documenting something most people would want to change is very very easy to overlook.  That\'s what I call a \u003cem\u003etrap\u003c\\/em\u003e; not that there might be some uses for the current behavior.  Lucene should do what most users want it do do by default.  As Jack said, the users of the search platform don\'t care what Java\'s definition of Character.isWhitespace is.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI propose WhitespaceTokenizerFactory have a flag for this, and that it default to consider NBSP a space based on Lucene\'s Version.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI get Uwe\'s point that there are other Tokenizers.  But I disagree that WhitespaceTokenizer shouldn\'t be used for \\\"classical full text\\\".  For example StandardTokenizer tokenizes on hypthen and thus foils some of the benefit of WordDelimiterFilter.  Maybe ICUTokenizer is an answer; I haven\'t checked it\'s interaction with WDF.  But why can\'t we just have a tokenizer that just tokenizes simply on all whitespace?\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI\'ll have to see the links Rob just posted; I haven\'t read them yet.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"dsmiley\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_14985598_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=dsmiley\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"dsmiley\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e David Smiley\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_14985598_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'02\\/Nov\\/15 17:43\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2015-11-02T17:43:09+0000\'\u003e02\\/Nov\\/15 17:43\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                     So maybe we should solve this problem by adding some documentation?  \\n\\n If the vast majority (like 90%+) of users that currently use WhitespaceTokenizer would want to tokenize on it, then I don\'t think documentation is sufficient at all.  Documenting something most people would want to change is very very easy to overlook.  That\'s what I call a  trap ; not that there might be some uses for the current behavior.  Lucene should do what most users want it do do by default.  As Jack said, the users of the search platform don\'t care what Java\'s definition of Character.isWhitespace is. \\n\\n I propose WhitespaceTokenizerFactory have a flag for this, and that it default to consider NBSP a space based on Lucene\'s Version. \\n\\n I get Uwe\'s point that there are other Tokenizers.  But I disagree that WhitespaceTokenizer shouldn\'t be used for \\\"classical full text\\\".  For example StandardTokenizer tokenizes on hypthen and thus foils some of the benefit of WordDelimiterFilter.  Maybe ICUTokenizer is an answer; I haven\'t checked it\'s interaction with WDF.  But why can\'t we just have a tokenizer that just tokenizes simply on all whitespace? \\n\\n I\'ll have to see the links Rob just posted; I haven\'t read them yet.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003eThen we could consider deprecating WhitespaceTokenizer since, after all, why would one use it when ICUWhitespaceTokenizer exists?\u003c\\/p\u003e\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eBecause the non-breaking space is useful for stuff (as explained above) where you want to keep tokens together (although usicode standard speaks about line wrapping, but in any case, like soft hyphen vs. hyphen, its just a matter what you want to do: the NBSP just tells the tokenizer or line-breaker or how you call it to keep tokens together). The problem are people that misuse \u003ctt\u003e&nbsp;\u003c\\/tt\u003e in their HTML shit (e.g. tables). But for stuff I had implemented very often, I used WhitepsaceTokenizer to split tokens and placed a non-breaking space to keep tokens together.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSo there is no need to deprecate WhitespaceTokenizer. It does what it should do. ICUWhitespaceTokenizer is using same naming and does the same, just with different rules.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003e... or consider a MappingCharFilter\u003c\\/p\u003e\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThis is thing is slow like hell. If you want it faster, e.g. use PatternTokenizer.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003eIt would be so nice to not need it, even if it\'s internal implementation seems fast\u003c\\/p\u003e\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThe problem is that you need to do additional 4-way branching: You have to check in \u003ctt\u003eisTokenChar()\u003c\\/tt\u003e that it is \u003ctt\u003e!Whitespace()\u003c\\/tt\u003e and also exclude all those 3 chars we listed in the description: \u003ctt\u003e\'\\\\u00A0\', \'\\\\u2007\', \'\\\\u202F\'\u003c\\/tt\u003e.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI agree with Robert: We should not change the default WhitespaceTokenizer and also not deprecate it. We should add a new one, which I did in supplied patch. If we want it in core, lets call it different and implement isTokenChar in a fast way without 3 additional branches.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003eI beg to differ on WDF\u003c\\/p\u003e\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThis is coming from the fact that Solr is often misused because users just give up to think about tokenization. WDF only makes sense in product catalogues, but it is definitely broken for fulltext. The product catalogues are of course some of our customers, but before I suggest to them that they should use WhiteSpaceTokenizer with WordDestroyerFilter, I would analyzer their root problem (why is their tokenization broken). This is why I am against the broken example configs in Solr we had in the past. Because WST and WDF should really only be used as a last resort.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"thetaphi\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_14985749_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=thetaphi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"thetaphi\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Uwe Schindler\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_14985749_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'02\\/Nov\\/15 18:53\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2015-11-02T18:53:06+0000\'\u003e02\\/Nov\\/15 18:53\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                     Then we could consider deprecating WhitespaceTokenizer since, after all, why would one use it when ICUWhitespaceTokenizer exists?  \\n\\n Because the non-breaking space is useful for stuff (as explained above) where you want to keep tokens together (although usicode standard speaks about line wrapping, but in any case, like soft hyphen vs. hyphen, its just a matter what you want to do: the NBSP just tells the tokenizer or line-breaker or how you call it to keep tokens together). The problem are people that misuse  &nbsp;  in their HTML shit (e.g. tables). But for stuff I had implemented very often, I used WhitepsaceTokenizer to split tokens and placed a non-breaking space to keep tokens together. \\n\\n So there is no need to deprecate WhitespaceTokenizer. It does what it should do. ICUWhitespaceTokenizer is using same naming and does the same, just with different rules. \\n\\n  ... or consider a MappingCharFilter  \\n\\n This is thing is slow like hell. If you want it faster, e.g. use PatternTokenizer. \\n\\n  It would be so nice to not need it, even if it\'s internal implementation seems fast  \\n\\n The problem is that you need to do additional 4-way branching: You have to check in  isTokenChar()  that it is  !Whitespace()  and also exclude all those 3 chars we listed in the description:  \'\\\\u00A0\', \'\\\\u2007\', \'\\\\u202F\' . \\n\\n I agree with Robert: We should not change the default WhitespaceTokenizer and also not deprecate it. We should add a new one, which I did in supplied patch. If we want it in core, lets call it different and implement isTokenChar in a fast way without 3 additional branches. \\n\\n  I beg to differ on WDF  \\n\\n This is coming from the fact that Solr is often misused because users just give up to think about tokenization. WDF only makes sense in product catalogues, but it is definitely broken for fulltext. The product catalogues are of course some of our customers, but before I suggest to them that they should use WhiteSpaceTokenizer with WordDestroyerFilter, I would analyzer their root problem (why is their tokenization broken). This is why I am against the broken example configs in Solr we had in the past. Because WST and WDF should really only be used as a last resort.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv id=\\\"comment-14985776\\\" class=\\\"issue-data-block activity-comment twixi-block  expanded\\\"\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap verbose actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Collapse comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-expanded\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eHide\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-links\\\"\u003e\\n                \u003ca href=\\\"\\/jira\\/browse\\/LUCENE-6874?focusedCommentId=14985776&page=com.atlassian.jira.plugin.system.issuetabpanels:comment-tabpanel#comment-14985776\\\"\\n                   title=\\\"Right click and copy link for a permanent link to this comment.\\\" class=\\\"activitymodule-link issue-comment-action\\\"\u003e\\n                    \u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-link\\\"\u003ePermalink\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n                                            \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details\\\"\u003e        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"steve_rowe\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_14985776_verbose\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=steve_rowe\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"steve_rowe\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Steve Rowe\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eOne thing to make it full flexible in Lucene Trunk (Java 8 only). I know this would not help Solr users that want to define the Tokenizer in a config file, but for real Lucene users the Java 8-like way would be the following static method on CharTokenizer:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"code panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"codeContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre class=\\\"code-java\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"code-keyword\\\"\u003epublic\u003c\\/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\\\"code-keyword\\\"\u003estatic\u003c\\/span\u003e CharTokenizer fromPredicate(java.util.function.IntPredicate predicate)\\n\u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThis would allow to define a new CharTokenizer with a single line statement using any predicate:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cdiv class=\\\"code panel\\\" style=\\\"border-width: 1px;\\\"\u003e\u003cdiv class=\\\"codeContent panelContent\\\"\u003e\\n\u003cpre class=\\\"code-java\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"code-comment\\\"\u003e\\/\\/ \u003cspan class=\\\"code-object\\\"\u003elong\u003c\\/span\u003e variant with lambda:\\n\u003c\\/span\u003eTokenizer tok = CharTokenizer.fromPredicate(c -&gt; !UCharacter.isUWhiteSpace(c));\\n\\n\u003cspan class=\\\"code-comment\\\"\u003e\\/\\/ method reference:\\n\u003c\\/span\u003eTokenizer tok = CharTokenizer.fromPredicate( (UCharacter::isUWhiteSpace).negate() );\\n\\n\u003cspan class=\\\"code-comment\\\"\u003e\\/\\/ method reference to custom function:\\n\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"code-keyword\\\"\u003eprivate\u003c\\/span\u003e \u003cspan class=\\\"code-object\\\"\u003eboolean\u003c\\/span\u003e myTestFunction(\u003cspan class=\\\"code-object\\\"\u003eint\u003c\\/span\u003e c) {\\n \u003cspan class=\\\"code-keyword\\\"\u003ereturn\u003c\\/span\u003e (cracy condition);\\n}\\n\\nTokenizer tok = CharTokenizer.fromPredicate(\u003cspan class=\\\"code-keyword\\\"\u003ethis\u003c\\/span\u003e::myTestFunction);\\n\u003c\\/pre\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI think we should do this in a separate issue in Lucene trunk for Java 8. This is really the way for which Java 8 Lambdas are made for. And its fast like hell, because its compiled to native bytecode so there is no call overhead.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n                                            \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"thetaphi\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_14985885_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=thetaphi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"thetaphi\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Uwe Schindler\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_14985885_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'02\\/Nov\\/15 19:43\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2015-11-02T19:43:06+0000\'\u003e02\\/Nov\\/15 19:43\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e   - \u003cspan class=\\\"redText subText\\\" title=\\\"Uwe Schindler - 02\\/Nov\\/15 19:44\\\"\u003eedited\u003c\\/span\u003e                   One thing to make it full flexible in Lucene Trunk (Java 8 only). I know this would not help Solr users that want to define the Tokenizer in a config file, but for real Lucene users the Java 8-like way would be the following static method on CharTokenizer: \\n\\n  \\n  public   static  CharTokenizer fromPredicate(java.util.function.IntPredicate predicate)\\n \\n  \\n\\n This would allow to define a new CharTokenizer with a single line statement using any predicate: \\n\\n  \\n  \\/\\/  long  variant with lambda:\\n Tokenizer tok = CharTokenizer.fromPredicate(c -&gt; !UCharacter.isUWhiteSpace(c));\\n\\n \\/\\/ method reference:\\n Tokenizer tok = CharTokenizer.fromPredicate( (UCharacter::isUWhiteSpace).negate() );\\n\\n \\/\\/ method reference to custom function:\\n  private   boolean  myTestFunction( int  c) {\\n  return  (cracy condition);\\n}\\n\\nTokenizer tok = CharTokenizer.fromPredicate( this ::myTestFunction);\\n \\n  \\n\\n I think we should do this in a separate issue in Lucene trunk for Java 8. This is really the way for which Java 8 Lambdas are made for. And its fast like hell, because its compiled to native bytecode so there is no call overhead.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n Rowe\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_14987389_verbose subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'03\\/Nov\\/15 14:45\'\u003e\u003ctime \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003ePatch adding a JFlex-based UnicodeWhitespaceTokenizer(Factory), along with some performance testing bits, some of which aren\'t commitable (hard-coded paths).  Also includes the SPI entry missing from Uwe\'s patch for \u003ctt\u003eICUWhitespaceTokenizerFactory\u003c\\/tt\u003e in \u003ctt\u003elucene\\/icu\\/src\\/resources\\/META-INF\\/services\\/o.a.l.analysis.util.TokenizerFactory\u003c\\/tt\u003e, as well as a couple bugfixes for \u003ctt\u003elucene\\/benchmark\u003c\\/tt\u003e (which I\'ll commit under a separate JIRA).  The patch also includes all of Uwe\'s patch.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI did three performance comparisons on my Macbook Pro with Oracle Java 1.8.0_20 of the \u003ctt\u003eCharacter.isWhitespace()\u003c\\/tt\u003e-based \u003ctt\u003eWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e, Uwe\'s \u003ctt\u003eICUWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e, and the JFlex \u003ctt\u003eUnicodeWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e1. Using the \u003ctt\u003ewstok.alg\u003c\\/tt\u003e in the patch, I ran \u003ctt\u003elucene\\/benchmark\u003c\\/tt\u003e over 20k (English news) Reuters docs: dropping the lowest throughput of 5 rounds and averaging the other 4:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cdiv class=\'table-wrap\'\u003e\\n\u003ctable class=\'confluenceTable\'\u003e\u003ctbody\u003e\\n\u003ctr\u003e\\n\u003cth class=\'confluenceTh\'\u003eTokenizer\u003c\\/th\u003e\\n\u003cth class=\'confluenceTh\'\u003eAvg tok\\/sec\u003c\\/th\u003e\\n\u003cth class=\'confluenceTh\'\u003eThroughput compared to \u003ctt\u003eWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e\u003c\\/th\u003e\\n\u003c\\/tr\u003e\\n\u003ctr\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e\u003ctt\u003eWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e1.515M\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003eN\\/A\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003c\\/tr\u003e\\n\u003ctr\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e\u003ctt\u003eICUWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e1.447M\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e\u003cfont color=\\\"red\\\"\u003e-5.5%\u003c\\/font\u003e\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003c\\/tr\u003e\\n\u003ctr\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e\u003ctt\u003eUnicodeWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e1.514M\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e\u003cfont color=\\\"red\\\"\u003e-0.1%\u003c\\/font\u003e\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003c\\/tr\u003e\\n\u003c\\/tbody\u003e\u003c\\/table\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e2. I concatenated all ~20k Reuters docs into one file, loaded it into memory and then ran each tokenizer over it 11 times, discarding info from the first and averaging the other 10 (this is \u003ctt\u003etestReuters()\u003c\\/tt\u003e in the \u003ctt\u003eTest*\u003c\\/tt\u003e files in the patch:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cdiv class=\'table-wrap\'\u003e\\n\u003ctable class=\'confluenceTable\'\u003e\u003ctbody\u003e\\n\u003ctr\u003e\\n\u003cth class=\'confluenceTh\'\u003eTokenizer\u003c\\/th\u003e\\n\u003cth class=\'confluenceTh\'\u003eAvg tok\\/sec\u003c\\/th\u003e\\n\u003cth class=\'confluenceTh\'\u003eThroughput compared to \u003ctt\u003eWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e\u003c\\/th\u003e\\n\u003c\\/tr\u003e\\n\u003ctr\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e\u003ctt\u003eWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e14.47M\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003eN\\/A\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003c\\/tr\u003e\\n\u003ctr\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e\u003ctt\u003eICUWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e9.26M\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e\u003cfont color=\\\"red\\\"\u003e-36%\u003c\\/font\u003e\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003c\\/tr\u003e\\n\u003ctr\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e\u003ctt\u003eUnicodeWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e11.60M\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e\u003cfont color=\\\"red\\\"\u003e-20%\u003c\\/font\u003e\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003c\\/tr\u003e\\n\u003c\\/tbody\u003e\u003c\\/table\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003e3. I used a fixed random seed and generated 10k random Unicode strings of at most 10k chars using \u003ctt\u003eTestUtil.randomUnicodeString()\u003c\\/tt\u003e.  Note that this is non-realistic data for tokenization, not least because the average whitespace density is very low compared to natural language.  In running this test I noticed that \u003ctt\u003eWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e was returning many more tokens than the other two, and I tracked it down to differences in the definition of whitespace:\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cul\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003e\u003ctt\u003eCharacter.isWhitespace()\u003c\\/tt\u003e returns true for the following while Unicode 6.3.0 (Lucene\'s current Unicode version) does not: U+001C, U+001D, U+001E, U+001F, U+0180E.  (U+0180E was removed from Unicode\'s whitespace definition in Unicode 6.3.0. Java 8 uses Unicode 6.2.0.)\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\\t\u003cli\u003eUnicode 6.3.0 says the following are whitespace while \u003ctt\u003eCharacter.isWhitespace()\u003c\\/tt\u003e does not: U+0085, U+00A0, U+2007, U+202F.  The last 3 are documented, but U+0085 \u003ctt\u003eNEXT LINE (NEL)\u003c\\/tt\u003e isn\'t documented anywhere I can see; it was added to Unicode\'s whitespace definition in Unicode 3.0 (released 2001).\u003c\\/li\u003e\\n\u003c\\/ul\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eSo in order to be able to directly compare the performance of three tokenizers over this data, I replaced all non-consensus whitespace characters with a space before running the test.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cdiv class=\'table-wrap\'\u003e\\n\u003ctable class=\'confluenceTable\'\u003e\u003ctbody\u003e\\n\u003ctr\u003e\\n\u003cth class=\'confluenceTh\'\u003eTokenizer\u003c\\/th\u003e\\n\u003cth class=\'confluenceTh\'\u003eAvg tok\\/sec\u003c\\/th\u003e\\n\u003cth class=\'confluenceTh\'\u003eThroughput compared to \u003ctt\u003eWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e\u003c\\/th\u003e\\n\u003c\\/tr\u003e\\n\u003ctr\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e\u003ctt\u003eWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e897k\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003eN\\/A\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003c\\/tr\u003e\\n\u003ctr\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e\u003ctt\u003eICUWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e880k\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e\u003cfont color=\\\"red\\\"\u003e-2%\u003c\\/font\u003e\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003c\\/tr\u003e\\n\u003ctr\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e\u003ctt\u003eUnicodeWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e1,605k\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003ctd class=\'confluenceTd\'\u003e\u003cfont color=\\\"green\\\"\u003e+79%\u003c\\/font\u003e\u003c\\/td\u003e\\n\u003c\\/tr\u003e\\n\u003c\\/tbody\u003e\u003c\\/table\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eOne other thing I noticed for this test when I compared \u003ctt\u003eICUWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e\'s output with that of \u003ctt\u003eUnicodeWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e\'s: they don\'t always find the same break points.  This is because although both forcibly break at the max token length (255 chars, fixed for \u003ctt\u003eCharTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e and the default for Lucene\'s JFlex scanners), \u003ctt\u003eCharTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e allows tokens to exceed its max token char length of 255 by one char when a surrogate pair would otherwise be broken, while Lucene\'s JFlex scanners break at 254 chars in this case. \u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003chr \\/\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eConclusion: for throughput over realistic ASCII data, the original \u003ctt\u003eWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e performs best, followed by the JFlex-based tokenizer in this patch (\u003ctt\u003eUnicodeWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e), followed by the ICU-based \u003ctt\u003eICUWhitespaceTokenizer\u003c\\/tt\u003e in Uwe\'s patch.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"steve_rowe\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_14987389_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=steve_rowe\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"steve_rowe\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Steve Rowe\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_14987389_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'03\\/Nov\\/15 14:45\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2015-11-03T14:45:21+0000\'\u003e03\\/Nov\\/15 14:45\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Patch adding a JFlex-based UnicodeWhitespaceTokenizer(Factory), along with some performance testing bits, some of which aren\'t commitable (hard-coded paths).  Also includes the SPI entry missing from Uwe\'s patch for  ICUWhitespaceTokenizerFactory  in  lucene\\/icu\\/src\\/resources\\/META-INF\\/services\\/o.a.l.analysis.util.TokenizerFactory , as well as a couple bugfixes for  lucene\\/benchmark  (which I\'ll commit under a separate JIRA).  The patch also includes all of Uwe\'s patch. \\n\\n I did three performance comparisons on my Macbook Pro with Oracle Java 1.8.0_20 of the  Character.isWhitespace() -based  WhitespaceTokenizer , Uwe\'s  ICUWhitespaceTokenizer , and the JFlex  UnicodeWhitespaceTokenizer : \\n\\n 1. Using the  wstok.alg  in the patch, I ran  lucene\\/benchmark  over 20k (English news) Reuters docs: dropping the lowest throughput of 5 rounds and averaging the other 4: \\n\\n \\n  \\n \\n Tokenizer \\n Avg tok\\/sec \\n Throughput compared to  WhitespaceTokenizer  \\n \\n \\n  WhitespaceTokenizer  \\n 1.515M \\n N\\/A \\n \\n \\n  ICUWhitespaceTokenizer  \\n 1.447M \\n  -5.5%  \\n \\n \\n  UnicodeWhitespaceTokenizer  \\n 1.514M \\n  -0.1%  \\n \\n  \\n \\n\\n\\n 2. I concatenated all ~20k Reuters docs into one file, loaded it into memory and then ran each tokenizer over it 11 times, discarding info from the first and averaging the other 10 (this is  testReuters()  in the  Test*  files in the patch: \\n\\n \\n  \\n \\n Tokenizer \\n Avg tok\\/sec \\n Throughput compared to  WhitespaceTokenizer  \\n \\n \\n  WhitespaceTokenizer  \\n 14.47M \\n N\\/A \\n \\n \\n  ICUWhitespaceTokenizer  \\n 9.26M \\n  -36%  \\n \\n \\n  UnicodeWhitespaceTokenizer  \\n 11.60M \\n  -20%  \\n \\n  \\n \\n\\n\\n 3. I used a fixed random seed and generated 10k random Unicode strings of at most 10k chars using  TestUtil.randomUnicodeString() .  Note that this is non-realistic data for tokenization, not least because the average whitespace density is very low compared to natural language.  In running this test I noticed that  WhitespaceTokenizer  was returning many more tokens than the other two, and I tracked it down to differences in the definition of whitespace: \\n\\n \\n\\t  Character.isWhitespace()  returns true for the following while Unicode 6.3.0 (Lucene\'s current Unicode version) does not: U+001C, U+001D, U+001E, U+001F, U+0180E.  (U+0180E was removed from Unicode\'s whitespace definition in Unicode 6.3.0. Java 8 uses Unicode 6.2.0.) \\n\\t Unicode 6.3.0 says the following are whitespace while  Character.isWhitespace()  does not: U+0085, U+00A0, U+2007, U+202F.  The last 3 are documented, but U+0085  NEXT LINE (NEL)  isn\'t documented anywhere I can see; it was added to Unicode\'s whitespace definition in Unicode 3.0 (released 2001). \\n \\n\\n\\n So in order to be able to directly compare the performance of three tokenizers over this data, I replaced all non-consensus whitespace characters with a space before running the test. \\n\\n \\n  \\n \\n Tokenizer \\n Avg tok\\/sec \\n Throughput compared to  WhitespaceTokenizer  \\n \\n \\n  WhitespaceTokenizer  \\n 897k \\n N\\/A \\n \\n \\n  ICUWhitespaceTokenizer  \\n 880k \\n  -2%  \\n \\n \\n  UnicodeWhitespaceTokenizer  \\n 1,605k \\n  +79%  \\n \\n  \\n \\n\\n\\n One other thing I noticed for this test when I compared  ICUWhitespaceTokenizer \'s output with that of  UnicodeWhitespaceTokenizer \'s: they don\'t always find the same break points.  This is because although both forcibly break at the max token length (255 chars, fixed for  CharTokenizer  and the default for Lucene\'s JFlex scanners),  CharTokenizer  allows tokens to exceed its max token char length of 255 by one char when a surrogate pair would otherwise be broken, while Lucene\'s JFlex scanners break at 254 chars in this case.  \\n\\n \\n\\n Conclusion: for throughput over realistic ASCII data, the original  WhitespaceTokenizer  performs best, followed by the JFlex-based tokenizer in this patch ( UnicodeWhitespaceTokenizer ), followed by the ICU-based  ICUWhitespaceTokenizer  in Uwe\'s patch.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n\u003c\\/div\u003e\\n                             \\n\\n\\n\u003cdiv class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2015-11-04T01:07:32+0000\'\u003e04\\/Nov\\/15 01:07\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003eBecause WST and WDF should really only be used as a last resort.\u003c\\/p\u003e\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAbsolutely agreed. From a Solr user perspective we really need a much simpler model for semi-standard tokens out of the box without the user having to scratch their heads and resorting to WST in the first (last) place. LOL - maybe if we could eliminate this need to resort to WST, we wouldn\'t have to fret as much about WST.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003eI generally suggest to my users to use ClassicTokenizer\u003c\\/p\u003e\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003ePersonally, I\'ve always refrained from recommending CT since I thought ST was supposed to replace it and that the email and URL support was considered an excess not worth keeping. I\'ve considered CT as if it were deprecated (which it is not.) And, I never see anybody else recommending it on the user list. And, the fact that it can\'t handle slashes for product number is a deal killer. I\'m not sure that I would argue in favor of resurrecting CT as a first-class recommendation, especially since it can\'t handle non-European languages, but...\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eThat said, I do think it is worth separately (from this Jira) considering a fresh, new tokenizer that starts with the goodness of ST and adds in an approximation of the reasons that people resort to WST. Whether that can be an option on ST or has to be a separate tokenizer would need to be debated. I\'d prefer an option on ST, either to simply allow embedded special characters or to specify a list or regex of special character to be allowed or excluded.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003ePeople would still need to combine NewT with WDF, but at least the tokenization would be more explicit.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003ePersonally I would prefer to see an option for whether to retain or strip external punctuation vs. embedded special characters. Trailing periods and commas and columns and enclosing parentheses are just the kinds of things we had to resort to WDF for when using WST to retain embedded special characters.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eAnd if people really want to be ambitious, a totally new tokenizer that subsumed the good parts of WDF would make a lot of lives of Solr users much easier.\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"jkrupan\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_14988646_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=jkrupan\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"jkrupan\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e Jack Krupansky\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_14988646_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'04\\/Nov\\/15 01:07\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2015-11-04T01:07:32+0000\'\u003e04\\/Nov\\/15 01:07\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                     Because WST and WDF should really only be used as a last resort.  \\n\\n Absolutely agreed. From a Solr user perspective we really need a much simpler model for semi-standard tokens out of the box without the user having to scratch their heads and resorting to WST in the first (last) place. LOL - maybe if we could eliminate this need to resort to WST, we wouldn\'t have to fret as much about WST. \\n\\n  I generally suggest to my users to use ClassicTokenizer  \\n\\n Personally, I\'ve always refrained from recommending CT since I thought ST was supposed to replace it and that the email and URL support was considered an excess not worth keeping. I\'ve considered CT as if it were deprecated (which it is not.) And, I never see anybody else recommending it on the user list. And, the fact that it can\'t handle slashes for product number is a deal killer. I\'m not sure that I would argue in favor of resurrecting CT as a first-class recommendation, especially since it can\'t handle non-European languages, but... \\n\\n That said, I do think it is worth separately (from this Jira) considering a fresh, new tokenizer that starts with the goodness of ST and adds in an approximation of the reasons that people resort to WST. Whether that can be an option on ST or has to be a separate tokenizer would need to be debated. I\'d prefer an option on ST, either to simply allow embedded special characters or to specify a list or regex of special character to be allowed or excluded. \\n\\n People would still need to combine NewT with WDF, but at least the tokenization would be more explicit. \\n\\n Personally I would prefer to see an option for whether to retain or strip external punctuation vs. embedded special characters. Trailing periods and commas and columns and enclosing parentheses are just the kinds of things we had to resort to WDF for when using WST to retain embedded special characters. \\n\\n And if people really want to be ambitious, a totally new tokenizer that subsumed the good parts of WDF would make a lot of lives of Solr users much easier.              \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2015-11-04T02:54:44+0000\'\u003e04\\/Nov\\/15 02:54\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e  \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-body flooded\\\"\u003e\u003cp\u003eJack:  My use-case since you asked:  I\'ve got a document store of content in XML that provides various markup around mostly text.  These documents occasionally have an NBSP.  I process it outside of Solr to produce the text I want indexed\\/stored &#8211; it\'s not XML any more.  An NBSP entity, if found, is converted to the NBSP character naturally as part of Java\'s XML libraries (no explicit decision on my part).\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cblockquote\u003e\u003cp\u003eImplicitly then, you\'re nixing ICUWhitespaceTokenizer, since it can\'t be in analyzers-common.\u003c\\/p\u003e\u003c\\/blockquote\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eRight; ah well.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eRE what to name the attribute:  I suggest \\\"definition\\\" or even better: \\\"rule\\\" (or \\\"ruleset\\\")\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eI do think the first-line sentence of these whitespace tokenizers should point to what definition of whitespace is chosen.  And that they reference each other so that anyone stumbling on them will know of the other.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eRE WDF:  I prefer WhitespaceTokenizer with WDF for not just product-id data but also full-text.  Full-text might contain product-ids, or have things like \\\"wi-fi\\\" and many other words, like say \\\"thread-safe\\\" or \\\"co-worker\\\" that are sometimes hyphenated, sometimes not; some of these might be space-separated; etc..  WDF is very flexible but if you use a Tokenizer like Standard* or Classic* then hyphen will be pre-tokenized before WDF can do its thing, neutering part of its benefit.  I wish WDF kept payloads and other attributes; but it\'s not the only offender here, and likewise for the bigger issue of positionLength.  Otherwise I\'m a WDF fan \u003cimg class=\\\"emoticon\\\" src=\\\"\\/jira\\/images\\/icons\\/emoticons\\/smile.png\\\" height=\\\"16\\\" width=\\\"16\\\" align=\\\"absmiddle\\\" alt=\\\"\\\" border=\\\"0\\\"\\/\u003e  Nonetheless I like some of Jack\'s ideas on a better tokenizer that subsumes WDF.\u003c\\/p\u003e\\n\\n\u003cp\u003eBTW, FWIW if I had to write a WhitespaceTokenizer from scratch, I\'d implement it as a bitset for characters &lt; 65k (this is 8KB memory).  For the remainder I\'d use an array that is scanned; but it appears there are none beyond 65k as I look at a table of these char\'s from a quick google search.  Then a configurable definition loader could fill named whitespace rules and it might be configurable to add or remove certain codes.  But no need to bother; Steve\'s impl is fine \u003cimg class=\\\"emoticon\\\" src=\\\"\\/jira\\/images\\/icons\\/emoticons\\/smile.png\\\" height=\\\"16\\\" width=\\\"16\\\" align=\\\"absmiddle\\\" alt=\\\"\\\" border=\\\"0\\\"\\/\u003e\u003c\\/p\u003e \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003c\\/div\u003e\\n    \u003cdiv class=\\\"twixi-wrap concise actionContainer\\\"\u003e\\n        \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-head\\\"\u003e\\n            \u003ca href=\\\"#\\\" title=\\\"Expand comment\\\" class=\\\"twixi\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"icon-default aui-icon aui-icon-small aui-iconfont-collapsed\\\"\u003e\u003cspan\u003eShow\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n            \u003cdiv class=\\\"action-details flooded\\\"\u003e\\n                        \\n    \\n    \\n    \\n                \\n\\n    \u003ca class=\\\"user-hover user-avatar\\\" rel=\\\"dsmiley\\\" id=\\\"commentauthor_14988791_concise\\\" href=\\\"\\/jira\\/secure\\/ViewProfile.jspa?name=dsmiley\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar aui-avatar-xsmall\\\"\u003e\u003cspan class=\\\"aui-avatar-inner\\\"\u003e\u003cimg src=\\\"https:\\/\\/issues.apache.org\\/jira\\/secure\\/useravatar?size=xsmall&amp;avatarId=10452\\\" alt=\\\"dsmiley\\\" \\/\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e David Smiley\u003c\\/a\u003e\\n added a comment  - \u003cspan class=\'commentdate_14988791_concise subText\'\u003e\u003cspan class=\'date user-tz\' title=\'04\\/Nov\\/15 02:54\'\u003e\u003ctime class=\'livestamp\' datetime=\'2015-11-04T02:54:44+0000\'\u003e04\\/Nov\\/15 02:54\u003c\\/time\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e\u003c\\/span\u003e                    Jack:  My use-case since you asked:  I\'ve got a document store of content in XML that provides various markup around mostly text.  These documents occasionally have an NBSP.  I process it outside of Solr to produce the text I want indexed\\/stored &#8211; it\'s not XML any more.  An NBSP entity, if found, is converted to the NBSP character naturally as part of Java\'s XML libraries (no explicit decision on my part). \\n\\n  Implicitly then, you\'re nixing ICUWhitespaceTokenizer, since it can\'t be in analyzers-common.  \\n\\n Right; ah well. \\n\\n RE what to name the attribute:  I suggest \\\"definition\\\" or even better: \\\"rule\\\" (or \\\"ruleset\\\") \\n\\n I do think the first-line sentence of these whitespace tokenizers should point to what definition of whitespace is chosen.  And that they reference each other so that anyone stumbling on them will know of the other. \\n\\n RE WDF:  I prefer WhitespaceTokenizer with WDF for not just product-id data but also full-text.  Full-text might contain product-ids, or have things like \\\"wi-fi\\\" and many other words, like say \\\"thread-safe\\\" or \\\"co-worker\\\" that are sometimes hyphenated, sometimes not; some of these might be space-separated; etc..  WDF is very flexible but if you use a Tokenizer like Standard* or Classic* then hyphen will be pre-tokenized before WDF can do its thing, neutering part of its benefit.  I wish WDF kept payloads and other attributes; but it\'s not the only offender here, and likewise for the bigger issue of positionLength.  Otherwise I\'m a WDF fan    Nonetheless I like some of Jack\'s ideas on a better tokenizer that subsumes WDF. \\n\\n BTW, FWIW if I had to write a WhitespaceTokenizer from scratch, I\'d implement it as a bitset for characters &lt; 65k (this is 8KB memory).  For the remainder I\'d use an array that is scanned; but it appears there are none beyond 65k as I look at a table of these char\'s from a quick google search.  Then a configurable definition loader could fill named whitespace rules and it might be configurable to add or remove certain codes.
